2.1	O
Early	O
Ideas	O
in	O
Atomic	O
Theory	EOS
By	O
the	O
end	O
of	O
this	O
section,	O
you	O
will	O
be	O
able	O
to:	EOS
State	O
the	O
postulates	O
of	O
Dalton’s	O
atomic	O
theory	EOS
Use	O
postulates	O
of	O
Dalton’s	O
atomic	O
theory	O
to	O
explain	O
the	O
laws	O
of	O
definite	O
and	O
multiple	O
proportions	EOS

The	O
earliest	O
recorded	O
discussion	O
of	O
the	O
basic	O
structure	O
of	O
matter	O
comes	O
from	O
ancient	O
Greek	O
philosophers,	O
the	O
scientists	O
of	O
their	O
day.	EOS
In	O
the	O
fifth	O
century	O
BC,	O
Leucippus	O
and	O
Democritus	O
argued	O
that	O
all	O
matter	O
was	O
composed	O
of	O
small,	O
finite	O
particles	O
that	O
they	O
called	O
atomos,	O
a	O
term	O
derived	O
from	O
the	O
Greek	O
word	O
for	O
“indivisible.”	EOS
They	O
thought	O
of	O
atoms	O
as	O
moving	O
particles	O
that	O
differed	O
in	O
shape	O
and	O
size,	O
and	O
which	O
could	O
join	O
together.	EOS
Later,	O
Aristotle	O
and	O
others	O
came	O
to	O
the	O
conclusion	O
that	O
matter	O
consisted	O
of	O
various	O
combinations	O
of	O
the	O
four	O
“elements”	O
—fire,	O
earth,	O
air,	O
and	O
water—and	O
could	O
be	O
infinitely	O
divided.	EOS
Interestingly,	O
these	O
philosophers	O
thought	O
about	O
atoms	O
and	O
“elements”	O
as	O
philosophical	O
concepts,	O
but	O
apparently	O
never	O
considered	O
performing	O
experiments	O
to	O
test	O
their	O
ideas.	EOS

The	O
Aristotelian	O
view	O
of	O
the	O
composition	O
of	O
matter	O
held	O
sway	O
for	O
over	O
two	O
thousand	O
years,	O
until	O

schoolteacher	O
John	O
Dalton	O
helped	O
to	O
revolutionize	O

with	O
his	O
hypothesis	O
that	O
the	O
behavior	O
of	O

could	O
be	O
explained	O
using	O
an	O
atomic	O
theory.	EOS
First	O
published	O
in	O
1807,	O
many	O
of	O
Dalton’s	O
hypotheses	O
about	O
the	O
microscopic	O
features	O
of	O
matter	O
are	O
still	O
valid	O
in	O
modern	O
atomic	O
theory.	EOS
Here	O
are	O
the	O
postulates	O
of	O
Dalton’s	O
atomic	O
theory.	EOS
1.	O
Matter	O
is	O
composed	O
of	O
exceedingly	O
small	O
particles	O
called	O
atoms.	EOS
An	O
atom	O
is	O
the	O
smallest	O
unit	O
of	O
an	O
element	O
that	O
can	O
participate	O
in	O
a	O
chemical	O
change.	EOS
2.	O
An	O
element	O
consists	O
of	O
only	O
one	O
type	O
of	O
atom,	O
which	O
has	O
a	O
mass	O
that	O
is	O
characteristic	O
of	O
the	O
element	O
and	O
is	O
the	O
same	O
for	O
all	O
atoms	O
of	O
that	O
element	O
(Figure	O
2.2).	EOS

A	O
macroscopic	O
sample	O
of	O
an	O
element	O
contains	O
an	O
incredibly	O
large	O
number	O
of	O
atoms,	O
all	O
of	O
which	O
have	O
identical	O
chemical	O
properties.	EOS

Dalton’s	O
atomic	O
theory	O
provides	O
a	O

of	O
the	O

a	O

2.1	EOS

Solution	EOS

and	O
two	O

(In	O

to	O

Your	O
Learning	EOS
In	O
the	O

How	O

The	O

can	O

Method	O
1	O
of	O
2:	O
From	O

Be	O

Method	O
2	O
of	O
2:	O
From	O
Cuttings	EOS
Obtain	O
Beavertail	O
cuttings.	EOS
You	O
can	O

online	O

at	O
a	O
local	O
garden	O

can	O
make	O

about	O
an	O
inch	O
(2.5	O
cm.)	O
deep.	EOS
If	O

too	O

they	O
might	O
rot.	EOS
Put	O
some	O

pad	O
to	O
anchor	O
it	O
in	O
place.	EOS
Choose	O
a	O
spot	O
for	O
your	O
Beavertail	O
cactus	O

If	O
you	O

This	O

Wait	O

Do	O
not	O

for	O

1	O

can	O
water	O
the	O
cutting	O
for	O
the	O
first	O

Always	O
let	O
the	O
soil	O
dry	O
before	O
you	O
water	O
the	O
cuttings.	EOS
Once	O
fully	O
rooted,	O
they	O
are	O
extremely	O
drought	O
resistant.	EOS
Fertilize	O
the	O
plants.	EOS
During	O
the	O
spring,	O

and	O

the	O
Beavertail	O

the	O

will	O

How	O
to	O
Get	O

of	O

Method	O
1	O

Many	O

in	O
places	O
that	O
are	O

mouse	O
attack.	O
[1]	EOS
Apply	O
peppermint	O
oil.	EOS
Peppermint	O
oil	O
is	O

is	O

[2]	EOS

[3]	EOS
